class="mw-body" role="main">\n\t<a id="top"></a>\n\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div>\n\t<div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n\t</div>\n\t<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" >Hawker Siddeley HS 748</h1>\n\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t<div id="contentSub2"></div>\n\t\t\n\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\n\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Airliner family by Hawker Siddeley, later British Aerospace</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n</p>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:25.5em;border-spacing:2px;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="2" style="text-align: center; font-size: large; padding-bottom: 0.3em;">HS 748\n</th></tr>\n\n\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/West_Air_Sweden" title="West Air Sweden">West Air Sweden</a> HS 748 Srs2/244\n</td></tr>\n\n<tr>\n<th>Role\n</th>\n<td>Airliner\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><span class="nowrap">National origin</span>\n</th>\n<td>United Kingdom\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Manufacturer\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Avro" title="Avro">Avro</a><br /> <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley" title="Hawker Siddeley">Hawker Siddeley</a> <br /><a 1960\n</td></tr>\n\n\n\n<tr>\n<th>Status\n</th>\n<td>Active service\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Primary&#160;users\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force" title="Indian Air Force">Indian Air Force</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Air_North" title="Air North">Air North</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Produced\n</th>\n<td>1961\xe2\x80\x931988\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><span class="nowrap">Number built</span>\n</th>\n<td>380\n</td></tr>\n\n<tr>\n<th>Variants\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_Andover" title="Hawker Siddeley Andover">Hawker Siddeley Andover</a><br /> <a href="/wiki/BAe_ATP" class="mw-redirect" title="BAe ATP">BAe ATP</a>\n</td></tr>\n\n</tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Hawker Siddeley HS 748</b> is a medium-sized <a href="/wiki/Turboprop" title="Turboprop">turboprop</a> <a href="/wiki/Airliner" title="Airliner">airliner</a> originally designed and initially produced by the British aircraft manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Avro" title="Avro">Avro</a>. It was the last aircraft to be developed by Avro prior to its absorption by Hawker Siddeley.\n</p><p>The HS 748 was developed during the late 1950s as a move to re-orientate the company towards the civil and export markets. Powered by the popular <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Dart" title="Rolls-Royce Dart">Rolls-Royce Dart</a> <a href="/wiki/Turboprop" title="Turboprop">turboprop</a> engine, it was specifically designed as a modern <a href="/wiki/Feederliner" class="mw-redirect" title="Feederliner">feederliner</a> to act as a replacement for the aging <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">Douglas DC-3s</a> then in widespread service. Originally intended to seat a smaller number of passengers, market research indicated that a seating capacity of around 40 passengers would be optimal for the type. As a means to differentiate the new airliner from competitors, it was designed to possess a high level of performance, including its <a href="/wiki/STOL" title="STOL">short takeoff and landing</a> (STOL) capabilities and overall ruggedness. First flying on 24 June 1960, the series 1 HS 748 entered revenue service during the following year.\n</p><p>Once in service, the HS 748 found itself a niche within the short-haul market. Several different models would be developed of the <a href="/wiki/Regional_airliner" title="Regional airliner">regional airliner</a>, typical improvements being the adoption of increasingly powerful Dart engines and a higher gross weight. Perhaps the most distinct variant was the <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_Andover" title="Hawker Siddeley Andover">HS 780 Andover</a>, a dedicated military transport model developed for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> (RAF) that featured a large rear loading ramp and a squatting main landing gear to assist in loading bulky freight items. By 1988, the year in which production of the type was terminated, 380 aircraft had been produced between <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley" title="Hawker Siddeley">Hawker Siddeley</a> (the owning company of Avro) and Indian aviation company <a href="/wiki/Hindustan_Aeronautics_Limited" title="Hindustan Aeronautics Limited">Hindustan Aeronautics Limited</a> (HAL). During the 1990s, a larger, stretched development of the HS 748, the <a href="/wiki/BAe_ATP" class="mw-redirect" title="BAe ATP">BAe ATP</a>, was developed and had attempted to compete with market leaders such as the <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Canada_Dash_8" title="De Havilland Canada Dash 8">de Havilland Canada Dash 8</a> and <a href="/wiki/ATR_42" title="ATR 42">ATR 42</a>, but saw only limited sales prior to production being terminated.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Siddeley_HS_748&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Siddeley_HS_748&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Following the release of the <a href="/wiki/1957_Defence_White_Paper" title="1957 Defence White Paper">1957 Defence White Paper</a>, in which then-<a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Minister of Defence (United Kingdom)">Minister of Defence</a> <a href="/wiki/Duncan_Sandys" title="Duncan Sandys">Duncan Sandys</a> announced that the termination of almost all manned military aircraft development, aircraft manufacturer Avro decided that it should place a greater emphasis upon the civilian market. Ten years prior, it had launched a civilian airliner, the <a href="/wiki/Avro_Tudor" title="Avro Tudor">Avro Tudor</a> series, but this had encountered few sales; thus, during 1958, it was decided to commence work upon a clean-sheet design, which would eventually become the HS 748. On 9 January 1959, the existence of the project, then referred to as the <i>Avro 748</i>, was announced to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_783_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_783-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By this point, the four-engined <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> had already secured the larger end of the short-haul market, therefore Avro decided that it would design a smaller <a href="/wiki/Regional_airliner" title="Regional airliner">regional airliner</a>, powered by a pair of <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Dart" title="Rolls-Royce Dart">Rolls-Royce Dart</a> <a href="/wiki/Turboprop" title="Turboprop">turboprop</a> engines. It was envisioned that this aircraft would be a suitable replacement for the many <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">DC-3 Dakotas</a> that were by then reaching the end of their economic lifespan. According to aviation periodical <a href="/wiki/Flight_International" title="Flight International">Flight International</a>, a major goal for the design team was to produce an aircraft that would be capable of operating from any airfield that the DC-3 could be.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_1342_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_1342-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Early intentions for the airliner was of a 20\xe2\x80\x9330 seat aircraft, adopting a somewhat similar configuration to the future rival <a href="/wiki/Fokker_F27_Friendship" title="Fokker F27 Friendship">Fokker F27 Friendship</a>; however, following discussions with several potential customers, the company opted for a low-wing 40-seat configuration. It was this latter arrangement that was chosen for the 748 project. Another important focus for the prospective airliner was compliance with both British and <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> standards of <a href="/wiki/Airworthiness" title="Airworthiness">airworthiness</a>; accordingly, it would be one of the first medium-sized aircraft to incorporate <a href="/wiki/Fail-safe" title="Fail-safe">fail-safe</a> design principles for its structure in place of the then-common <a href="/wiki/Safe-life_design" title="Safe-life design">safe-life</a> principles being practiced.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_1342_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_1342-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The airframe effectively lacked any imposed lifespan; during development, it was successfully tested using a <a href="/wiki/Water_tank" title="Water tank">water tank</a> for up to the equivalent of 100,000 flight hours.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_1342_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_1342-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Avro was not the only company to see the potential for a DC-3 replacement and, by this point, work on the 748\'s direct competitor, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a>-built F27 Friendship, was well advanced. To differentiate itself from the competition, Avro decided to focus its efforts upon achieving a more rugged design that offered superior <a href="/wiki/STOL" title="STOL">short takeoff and landing</a> (STOL) performance, which enabled the prospective airliner to be operated from smaller and more austere airports, including those without modern <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bae_heri_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bae_heri-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> This STOL capability was accomplished via several features, including the adoption of a long, <a href="/wiki/Aspect_ratio_(aeronautics)" title="Aspect ratio (aeronautics)">high lift wing</a>, which was fitted with a unique <a href="/wiki/Slotted_flap" class="mw-redirect" title="Slotted flap">single slot flap</a> with a hinged <a href="/wiki/Servo_tab" title="Servo tab">flap tab</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Trailing_edge" title="Trailing edge">trailing edge</a>. This wing was mounted low on the fuselage with <a href="/wiki/Dihedral_(aeronautics)" title="Dihedral (aeronautics)">dihedral</a> from the root, allowing for good overall ground clearance and the easy mounting of strong <a href="/wiki/Landing_gear" title="Landing gear">landing gear</a>. Operationally, pilots were provided with a choice of three takeoff flap settings to select the level of STOL performance required.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_1342_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_1342-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another supportive feature of the 748 was a design decision to adopt straightforward systems and use proven components where realistically possible.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_1342_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_1342-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> For operator convenience, the engines were provided with an internal ignition system; various other systems and structures throughout the airliner were designed to be easy to inspect and to perform repairs upon, even when at unprepared airstrips with limited equipment available. Likely as a consequence of these favourable qualities, the 748 quickly attracted the attention of a variety of airlines, particularly those that typically operated in remote areas, which has been attributed to its ability to operate from short rough fields without any ground service equipment while being capable of hauling <a href="/wiki/Payload" title="Payload">payloads</a> in excess of 10,000&#160;lb.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Into_flight">Into flight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Siddeley_HS_748&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Into flight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BKS_Avro_748_at_Manchester_1964.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/BKS_Avro_748_at_Manchester_1964.jpg/220px-BKS_Avro_748_at_Manchester_1964.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/BKS_Avro_748_at_Manchester_1964.jpg/330px-BKS_Avro_748_at_Manchester_1964.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/BKS_Avro_748_at_Manchester_1964.jpg/440px-BKS_Avro_748_at_Manchester_1964.jpg 2x" data-file-width="752" data-file-height="464" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BKS_Avro_748_at_Manchester_1964.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/BKS_Air_Transport" class="mw-redirect" title="BKS Air Transport">BKS Air Transport</a> Avro 748 Series 1 at Manchester in 1964</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HS748_LV-HHE_Aerolineas_Bs_As_26.04.72_edited-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/HS748_LV-HHE_Aerolineas_Bs_As_26.04.72_edited-2.jpg/220px-HS748_LV-HHE_Aerolineas_Bs_As_26.04.72_edited-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/HS748_LV-HHE_Aerolineas_Bs_As_26.04.72_edited-2.jpg/330px-HS748_LV-HHE_Aerolineas_Bs_As_26.04.72_edited-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/HS748_LV-HHE_Aerolineas_Bs_As_26.04.72_edited-2.jpg/440px-HS748_LV-HHE_Aerolineas_Bs_As_26.04.72_edited-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1057" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HS748_LV-HHE_Aerolineas_Bs_As_26.04.72_edited-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Aerolineas_Argentinas" class="mw-redirect" title="Aerolineas Argentinas">Aerolineas Argentinas</a> Avro 748 Series 1 at <a href="/wiki/Aeroparque_Jorge_Newbery" title="Aeroparque Jorge Newbery">Aeroparque Jorge Newbery</a>, Buenos Aires, in 1972</div></div></div>\n<p>On 24 June 1960, the first Avro 748 made its <a href="/wiki/Maiden_flight" title="Maiden flight">maiden flight</a> from the company\'s <a href="/wiki/Woodford_Aerodrome" title="Woodford Aerodrome">Woodford, Cheshire</a> aircraft factory.<sup id="cite_ref-bae_heri_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bae_heri-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Flight testing of the two prototypes quickly validated the type\'s short-field performance. Eighteen <i>Avro 748 Series 1</i> aircraft were produced; during April 1962, the first production aircraft were delivered to launch customer <a href="/wiki/Skyways_Coach-Air_Limited" title="Skyways Coach-Air Limited">Skyways Coach-Air Limited</a>. However, the majority of the series 1 were export sales to operator <a href="/wiki/Aerol%C3%ADneas_Argentinas" title="Aerol\xc3\xadneas Argentinas">Aerol\xc3\xadneas Argentinas</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> During the early 1960s, Avro\'s individual identity within the <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley" title="Hawker Siddeley">Hawker Siddeley</a> Group was expunged, after which the airliner was marketed by the parent company as the <i>HS 748</i>.\n</p><p>After the initial batch of series 1 aircraft was completed, production transitioned to the improved series 2. The series 2 was largely similar to its predecessor, principally benefiting from the adoption of more powerful <i>Dart RDa 7 Mk 531</i> engines and an increased gross weight. According to aviation periodical <a href="/wiki/Flight_International" title="Flight International">Flight International</a>, during 1960, the basic price for a new Avro 748 Series 1 was \xc2\xa3176,000, while that of the corresponding Avro 748 Series 2 was reportedly \xc2\xa3196,000.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_783_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_783-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During 1967, the series 2A was introduced, which was the same basic aircraft powered by <i>Mk. 532</i> engines along with a further increase in gross weight. From 1971 onwards, several new options were made available to customers, including a large freight door in the rear cabin and a strengthened cabin floor. During 1979, the Series 2B was introduced, which saw a 4-foot increase in <a href="/wiki/Wingspan" title="Wingspan">wingspan</a>, the adoption of <i>Mk 536-2</i> engines, along with a modernised passenger cabin, and various improvements to the fuel, <a href="/wiki/Water_injection_(engine)" title="Water injection (engine)">water methanol injection system</a>, and engine <a href="/wiki/Fire_suppression_system" title="Fire suppression system">fire protection systems</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>During 1976, Eric Johnson, sales engineering manager of Hawker Siddeley Manchester, stated that the company was studying options for equipping a model of the HS 748 with <a href="/wiki/Turbofan" title="Turbofan">turbofan</a> engines, and that a preferred powerplant at that point was the <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce/SNECMA_M45H" title="Rolls-Royce/SNECMA M45H">Rolls-Royce/SNECMA M45H</a>, as used on the <a href="/wiki/VFW-Fokker_614" title="VFW-Fokker 614">VFW-Fokker 614</a> jetliner.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_1342_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_1342-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Other changes would likely have been incorporated, including the addition of lift dumpers and adaptive brakes for better landing performance, while electrical, <a href="/wiki/Hydraulics" title="Hydraulics">hydraulic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Air_conditioning" title="Air conditioning">air conditioning</a> systems would be redesigned; externally, a dihedral would have to be introduced to keep the tailplane clear of the jet exhaust. It was envisioned that the reengined aircraft could offers larger seating arrangements of up to 64 seats.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_1342_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_1342-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition to the British production line, manufacture of the 748 was also performed overseas. Early on, India had placed orders for the type.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_783_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_783-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Both the 748 Series 1 and Series 2 were <a href="/wiki/Licensed_production" title="Licensed production">licence-produced</a> in Indian manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Hindustan_Aeronautics" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindustan Aeronautics">Hindustan Aeronautics</a> (HAL), aircraft produced by the company were designated <i>HAL-748</i>. On 1 November 1961, the first Indian-assembled HAL-748 made its first flight.<sup id="cite_ref-bae_heri_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bae_heri-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> By the end of production, HAL had completed 89 Indian-built aircraft, 72 of which were for the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force" title="Indian Air Force">Indian Air Force</a> and 17 were delivered to national <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/Indian_Airlines" title="Indian Airlines">Indian Airlines</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>While the HS 748 was originally intended to be marketed principally towards the civilian market, numerous examples were sold to military customers around the world. Hawker Siddeley used the design as the basis for the <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_Andover" title="Hawker Siddeley Andover">HS 780 Andover</a>, a military transport aircraft developed and produced for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>. In terms of its design, the HS 780 was broadly similar to the 748, differing primarily by its redesigned rear <a href="/wiki/Fuselage" title="Fuselage">fuselage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Empennage" title="Empennage">empennage</a>, which incorporated a large rear loading ramp and a squatting main landing gear to better facilitate the loading of bulky freight items.<sup id="cite_ref-bae_heri_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bae_heri-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During 1988, production of the HS 748 was terminated, while the last British-assembled aircraft made its first flight on 1 December of that year.<sup id="cite_ref-bae_heri_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bae_heri-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems" title="BAE Systems">BAE Systems</a>, a successor company to Hawker Siddeley, during the type\'s production life, a total of 381 aircraft had been produced, when including both the Andover and HAL-built examples.<sup id="cite_ref-bae_heri_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bae_heri-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operational_history">Operational history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Siddeley_HS_748&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Operational history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Siddeley_HS_748&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2019</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Within its first decade of its availability, sales of the HS 748 had reportedly been relatively brisk; by 1976, the sale of 312 aircraft had been recorded, of which 259 had been to export customers.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_1342_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_1342-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Within ten years of its launch, India had emerged as the largest single market for the airliner, <a href="/wiki/Indian_Airlines" title="Indian Airlines">Indian Airlines</a> being the largest HS 748 operator with a fleet of 26 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_1213_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_1213-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> It had been popular with numerous commercial operators, across the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> alone, 63 HS 748s were in operation with 11 separate operators.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_1213_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_1213-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The HS 748 had been able to achieve some triumphs over competing rivals, including the F27 Friendship. <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Airlines" title="Philippine Airlines">Philippine Airlines</a> had been the F27\'s largest operator prior to its decision to replace both it and its remaining DC-3s with the HS 748, which represented a significant sales coup for the latter.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_1342_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_1342-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Other major civil operators included <a href="/wiki/Aerolineas_Argentinas" class="mw-redirect" title="Aerolineas Argentinas">Aerolineas Argentinas</a>, <a href="/wiki/VARIG" class="mw-redirect" title="VARIG">VARIG</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thai_Airways" title="Thai Airways">Thai Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/LAN-Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="LAN-Chile">LAN-Chile</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bouraq_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Bouraq Airlines">Bouraq Airlines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bae_heri_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bae_heri-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Several of these operators would utilise its STOL capabilities in their services; according to Flight International, over one-third of all scheduled operations were reportedly involved operations from rough airstrips with minimalist facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_1213_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_1213-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another key market for the HS 748 was the <a href="/wiki/VIP" class="mw-redirect" title="VIP">executive</a> role; the type was repeatedly procured to serve as the designated aircraft for various <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">heads of state</a>, including of <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, India, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> and the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_1213_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_1213-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The HS 748 was one of the last planes to be flown by noted <a href="/wiki/Aviator" class="mw-redirect" title="Aviator">aviator</a> and <a href="/wiki/Business_magnate" title="Business magnate">business magnate</a> <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hughes" title="Howard Hughes">Howard Hughes</a>. During 1972, Hughes performed several flights of the type, each time accompanied by Hawker Siddeley test pilot Tony Blackman, flying from the company\'s airport in <a href="/wiki/Hatfield_Aerodrome" title="Hatfield Aerodrome">Hatfield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aero920p136_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aero920p136-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Australian military purchased several aircraft; specifically, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Australian_Air_Force" title="Royal Australian Air Force">Royal Australian Air Force</a> (RAAF) procured a fleet of ten HS 748s, the first of which arriving in 1968, for navigation training and transporting <a href="/wiki/VIP" class="mw-redirect" title="VIP">VIPs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aus_navy_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aus_navy-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Australian_Navy" title="Royal Australian Navy">Royal Australian Navy</a> (RAN) operated a pair of HS 748s starting in 1973 as a navigational trainer. Following <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Tracy" title="Cyclone Tracy">Cyclone Tracy</a>, relief aid was delivered across <a href="/wiki/Darwin,_Northern_Territory" title="Darwin, Northern Territory">Darwin, Northern Territory</a> using the type; after being fitted with various <a href="/wiki/Electronic_countermeasure" title="Electronic countermeasure">electronic countermeasures</a> (ECM) during the late 1970s, HS 748s were also used for <a href="/wiki/Electronic_warfare" title="Electronic warfare">electronic warfare</a> training.<sup id="cite_ref-aus_navy_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aus_navy-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In a typical passenger configuration, the HS 748 can accommodate around 40\xe2\x80\x9348 <a href="/wiki/Economy_class" title="Economy class">economy class</a> seats in a four abreast layout; however, the majority of later-serving passenger HS 748s were typically operated as quick change <i>combis</i>. These aircraft are fitted with a movable <a href="/wiki/Bulkhead_(partition)" title="Bulkhead (partition)">bulkhead</a> that divides the main cabin, housing between 4 and 40 seats in the rear section while cargo is placed the forward section.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_1213_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_1213-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The 748 has also been widely used as a pure freighter, having a typical max payload of about 12,000&#160;lbs. Several carriers have used the 748 as a bulk fuel hauler, in which capacity it is normally with either seven or eight fixed tanks in the cabin, possessing a total capacity of about 7,500&#160;L (1,600&#160;imp&#160;gal; 2,000&#160;US&#160;gal).<sup id="cite_ref-aero920p131_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aero920p131-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/ICAO" class="mw-redirect" title="ICAO">ICAO</a> designator as used in <a href="/wiki/Flight_plan" title="Flight plan">flight plans</a> is A748.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Variants">Variants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Siddeley_HS_748&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Variants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><b>748 Series 1</b> \xe2\x80\x93 The original Avro 748 twin-engined short / medium-range airliner, powered by two Rolls-Royce Dart RDa 7 Mk 514 turboprop engines. 24 built.<sup id="cite_ref-bae_heri_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bae_heri-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><span id="748_Series_2">748 Series 2</span></b> \xe2\x80\x93 The Series 2 entered production in 1961 with a higher take-off weight and Mk 531 engines. 111 built.</li>\n<li><b><span id="748_Series_2A">748 Series 2A</span></b> \xe2\x80\x93 Introduced in 1967, with a further increase in take-off weight and Mk 532 or 534 engines. 157 built, making the 748 one of the more successful British airliners and the 2A the most popular variant.</li>\n<li><b>748 Series 2B</b> \xe2\x80\x93 The main production model after Hawker-Siddeley was absorbed by British Aerospace, the 2B featured a 4-foot increase in wingspan, increased gross weight, Mk 536 engines, a modernized cabin, and systems improvements. 28 built.</li>\n<li><b>Super 748</b> \xe2\x80\x93 Basically the same as the 2B but fitted with engine hush kits. 8 Built.</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_HS780_Andover" class="mw-redirect" title="Hawker Siddeley HS780 Andover">Hawker Siddeley HS780 Andover</a></b> \xe2\x80\x93 Modified version of the 748 design for the Royal Air Force. Fitted with kneeling undercarriage, raised tail unit and rear loading ramp.</li>\n<li><b>Coastguarder</b> \xe2\x80\x93 A maritime patrol version.<sup id="cite_ref-bae_heri_3-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bae_heri-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>748 Andover</b> \xe2\x80\x93 Military passenger transport versions of the 748.<sup id="cite_ref-bae_heri_3-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bae_heri-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>HAL 748</b> \xe2\x80\x93 Licence production by Hindustan Aeronautics Limited at Bangalore India. Indian aircraft were later modified for a variety of roles including a trials aircraft for an <a href="/wiki/Airborne_Early_Warning" class="mw-redirect" title="Airborne Early Warning">Airborne Early Warning</a> version fitted with a large <a href="/wiki/Radome" title="Radome">radome</a>, known as the <a href="/wiki/Airborne_Surveillance_Platform" title="Airborne Surveillance Platform">Airborne Surveillance Platform</a> (ASP).<sup id="cite_ref-bae_heri_3-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bae_heri-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> 89 built.</li>\n<li><b>HAL 748 Series 2M</b> \xe2\x80\x93 Production for the Indian Air Force (the last 20 built) were Series 2M aircraft with a large freight door.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Siddeley_HS_748&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>On 10 July 1965, an Avro 748-101 Series 1 G-ARMV of <a href="/wiki/Skyways_Coach-Air" class="mw-redirect" title="Skyways Coach-Air">Skyways Coach-Air</a> was <a href="/wiki/1965_Skyways_Coach-Air_Avro_748_crash" title="1965 Skyways Coach-Air Avro 748 crash">written off in a landing accident</a> at <a href="/wiki/Lympne_Airport" title="Lympne Airport">Lympne Airport</a>. The 51 people on board survived. This was the first accident that resulted in a write-off on an Avro 748 / HS748.</li>\n<li>On 15 August 1967, two accidents involving HS-748-222 Series 2 aircraft of Channel Airways Limited, occurred roughly 90 minutes apart at Portsmouth Airport. In the first incident, G-ATEK, operating a scheduled service from Southend to Paris, via Portsmouth, landed in rainy conditions and was unable to stop in the available distance on the grass runway. The aircraft slid sideways, left the runway and stopped on an embankment. Some 90 minutes later, aircraft G-ATEH, operating a scheduled service from Jersey, via Guernsey to Portsmouth, landed and slid on the runway, crashed through a perimeter fence and came to rest on the main Eastern Road. There were no injuries in either accident, but both aircraft sustained serious damage. An AIB investigation<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> reported that "both accidents were caused by inadequate braking which had resulted from the extremely low coefficient of friction provided by the very wet grass surface over the hard, dry and almost impermeable sub-soil".</li>\n<li>On 4 February 1970, <a href="/wiki/Aerol%C3%ADneas_Argentinas_Flight_707" title="Aerol\xc3\xadneas Argentinas Flight 707">Aerol\xc3\xadneas Argentinas Flight 707</a>, an Avro 748\xe2\x80\x93105, crashed into the ground after the pilots lost control of the aircraft. The aircraft crashed at Loma Alta, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> and killed all 37 on board.</li>\n<li>On 9 December 1971, Indian Airlines, an HS 748, near Chinnamanur was descending into Madurai when it flew into high terrain about 50&#160;mi (80&#160;km) from the airport, killing the four crew members and 17 passengers. There were ten survivors among the passengers. The accident occurred in reduced visibility during daylight hours.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>20 January 1976 \xe2\x80\x93 a <a href="/wiki/TAME" title="TAME">TAME</a> HS 748-246 Series 2A registration HC-AUE crashed while flying over mountainous terrain at 10,000 feet. The aircraft struck trees with its right wing, lost control and crashed into the side of the mountain. The plane was en route from Loja to <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Joaqu%C3%ADn_de_Olmedo_International_Airport" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Joaqu\xc3\xadn de Olmedo International Airport">Sim\xc3\xb3n Bol\xc3\xadvar International Airport</a> in Guayaquil, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>. Six crewmembers and 28 passengers were killed; 8 passengers survived.</li>\n<li>3 March 1978 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/1978_LAV_HS_748_accident" title="1978 LAV HS 748 accident">L\xc3\xadnea Aeropostal Venezolana Hawker Siddeley HS 748</a> crashed on departure from <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_International_Airport_(Venezuela)" title="Sim\xc3\xb3n Bol\xc3\xadvar International Airport (Venezuela)">Sim\xc3\xb3n Bol\xc3\xadvar International Airport</a>, Venezuela, all 46 on board are killed.</li>\n<li>7 September 1978 \xe2\x80\x93 Air Ceylon HS 748 4R-ACJ destroyed by fire while parked at Colombo-Ratmalana, resulting from detonation of bomb placed on board by terrorists. There were no fatalities.</li>\n<li>31 July 1979 at Sumburgh Airport in the Shetland Islands, Scotland; <a href="/wiki/Dan-Air_Flight_0034" title="Dan-Air Flight 0034">Dan-Air Flight 0034</a>, an HS 748 series 1 (registration G-BEKF) operating an oil industry support flight crashed. The aircraft failed to become airborne and crashed into the sea. The accident was due to the elevator gust-lock having become re-engaged, preventing the aircraft from rotating into a flying attitude. The aircraft was destroyed and 17 persons died from drowning.</li>\n<li>4 August 1979 - The <a href="/wiki/Indian_Airlines" title="Indian Airlines">Indian Airlines</a> HAL-748 (VT-DXJ) was operating a scheduled flight from Pune to Bombay, India. The aircraft crashed in the Kiroli Hills near <a href="/wiki/Panvel" title="Panvel">Panvel</a> about 11 km east of Bombay. The aircraft was destroyed. All 45 persons on board were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>22 August 1979 \xe2\x80\x93 An <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_mechanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Aircraft mechanic">aircraft mechanic</a> (a former <a href="/wiki/Non-commissioned_officer" title="Non-commissioned officer">non-commissioned officer</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Air_Force" title="Colombian Air Force">Colombian Air Force</a>), stole a military HS 748 (<a href="/w/index.php?title=FAC-1101&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="FAC-1101 (page does not exist)">FAC-1101</a>) from a military hangar at the <a href="/wiki/Eldorado_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Eldorado International Airport">Eldorado International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogot\xc3\xa1">Bogot\xc3\xa1</a>, Colombia. According to the news, this person stole the aircraft with the intention of crashing it against his parents\' house. After some minutes in the air, it ran out of fuel and crashed, killing the impromptu pilot and three people on the ground.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>26 June 1981 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Dan-Air_Flight_240" title="Dan-Air Flight 240">Dan-Air Flight 240</a>, an HS 748 2A mail flight from <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a> to <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Airport" title="East Midlands Airport">East Midlands Airport</a> crashed at Nailstone killing the 3 crew members. While descending, the right-hand rear door detached, struck the horizontal tail plane and became lodged on its leading edge. Control was lost, and the aircraft entered a steep dive. During the dive, the wings and tail plane failed due to overstressing.</li>\n<li>19 August 1981 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Indian_Airlines" title="Indian Airlines">Indian Airlines</a> Flight 557, an HAL 748 (VT-DXF) overshot the runway at <a href="/wiki/Mangalore_International_Airport" title="Mangalore International Airport">Mangalore-Bajpe Airport</a> in wet weather. The aircraft came to a halt just beyond the runway edge. There were no fatalities but the damaged aircraft was written off. One of the passengers on board was <a href="/wiki/Veerappa_Moily" title="Veerappa Moily">Veerappa Moily</a> ex-Cabinet Minister for Law, Justice and Company Affairs in the Government of India.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>11 October 1983 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Air_Illinois_Flight_710" title="Air Illinois Flight 710">Air Illinois Flight 710</a> carrying 10 people crashed at night in a thunderstorm between Pinckneyville and Tamaroa, IL. The flight originated at Chicago\'s <a href="/wiki/Meigs_Field" title="Meigs Field">Meigs Field</a> and had stopped at Springfield, IL. The left generator had failed after takeoff and the first officer had mistakenly isolated the right generator. Attempts to restore the right generator were unsuccessful. The captain elected to continue to the destination rather than return to the nearby airport. The cloud base was at 2000 feet MSL, but ATC could not provide an IFR below 3,000 feet just before the crash. The crew indicated a total loss of electrical power. The left generator drive shaft had sheared.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> All ten passengers and crew were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>27 June 1987 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Airlines_Flight_206" title="Philippine Airlines Flight 206">Philippine Airlines Flight 206</a> crashed onto a mountain after poor visibility hampered the pilot\'s attempt to land at <a href="/wiki/Loakan_Airport" title="Loakan Airport">Loakan Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Baguio" title="Baguio">Baguio</a>, Philippines. All 50 passengers and crew were killed.</li>\n<li>10 November 1993 \xe2\x80\x93 Nothland Air Manitoba. Hawker Siddeley HS-748-234 Srs. 2A. Registration C-GQTH. Departure airport Sandy Lake Airport, Ontario (ZSJ/CZSJ), Canada "about 600&#160;km northeast of Winnipeg.". The aircraft took off from runway 29 at Sandy Lake at approximately 1805 and entered a right turn. Witnesses indicate that the aircraft appeared to fly at a lower than normal height throughout the turn. After turning through approximately 120 degrees, the aircraft descended into 100-foot trees and crashed. The aircraft struck the ground about 1&#160;nm northwest of the airport. Contributing factor was the loss of AC power to some of the flight instruments the reason for which could not be determined. All 3 crew members and 4 passengers perished.</li>\n<li>28 April 1995 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Air_Force_Avro_748_CR835" class="mw-redirect" title="Sri Lanka Air Force Avro 748 CR835">Sri Lanka Air Force Avro 748 CR835</a> an HS 748 serial CR835 (4R-HVB) was hit by an <a href="/wiki/SA-7" class="mw-redirect" title="SA-7">SA-7</a> missile fired by the <a href="/wiki/LTTE" class="mw-redirect" title="LTTE">LTTE</a> immediately after takeoff from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palaly/KKS/Jaffna&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Palaly/KKS/Jaffna (page does not exist)">Palaly/KKS/Jaffna</a>. All 45 occupants on board were killed. Crew managed to return the aircraft for landing but the starboard wing collapsed on short finals 295 meters from threshold due to an extensive fire in No-2 engine.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>11 January 1999 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/w/index.php?title=ASTE_HAL-748_ASP/H-2175&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ASTE HAL-748 ASP/H-2175 (page does not exist)">ASTE HAL-748 ASP/H-2175</a>, an HAL 748 crashed into the ground after the pilots lost control of the aircraft. The aircraft crashed at <a href="/wiki/Attur" title="Attur">Attur</a>, Tamil Nadu, India and killed the 2 crew and 6 passengers.</li>\n<li>5 September 1999 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Necon_Air_Flight_128" title="Necon Air Flight 128">Necon Air Flight 128</a> from Pokhara to Kathmandu, a BAe 748-501 Super 2B (9N-AEG), collided with a communication tower of Nepal Telecommunication Corporation and crashed in a wooded area 25&#160;km west of Kathmandu, while approaching Tribhuvan International Airport. All 10 passengers and 5 crew were killed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li>1 June 2002<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x93 Former South African cricket captain <a href="/wiki/Hansie_Cronje" title="Hansie Cronje">Hansie Cronje</a>\'s scheduled flight home from <a href="/wiki/Bloemfontein" title="Bloemfontein">Bloemfontein</a> to <a href="/wiki/George,_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="George, South Africa">George</a> had been grounded, so he hitched a ride as the only passenger on a cargo flight in an HS 748. Near George airport, the pilots lost visibility in cloud, and were unable to land, partly due to unserviceable navigational equipment. While circling, the plane crashed into the <a href="/wiki/Outeniqua_Mountains" title="Outeniqua Mountains">Outeniqua mountains</a> northeast of the airport. Cronje, aged 32, and the two pilots died. South Africa\'s High Court reached the conclusion that "the death of the deceased Wessel Johannes (Hansie) Cronje was brought about by an act or omission <a href="/wiki/Prima_facie" title="Prima facie">prima facie</a> amounting to an offence on the part of pilots."<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> However, with Cronje\'s involvement in match-fixing, theories that Cronje was murdered on the orders of a cricket betting syndicate flourished after his death.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>12 June 2012<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x93 A <a href="/wiki/Wasaya_Airways" title="Wasaya Airways">Wasaya Airways</a> Hawker Siddeley 748 caught fire during ground operations at Sandy Lake First Nation in Northwestern Ontario. No injuries were reported. The aircraft burned completely; only the left wing and nacelle survived.</li>\n<li>17 February 2014 \xe2\x80\x93 an HS 748-371 Srs 2B <a href="/wiki/2014_748_Air_Services_HS_748_crash" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 748 Air Services HS 748 crash">crash landed</a> at Rubkona airport in South Sudan killing one crew member and injuring the other three. The cargo plane was carrying humanitarian Aid to South Sudan.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>14 November 2014<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x93 A BAe HS-748 crashed on approach to <a href="/wiki/Panyagor" title="Panyagor">Panyagor</a> airstrip in South Sudan, killing two crew members and seriously injuring a third crew member. The cargo plane was on a charter flight for the Lutheran World Federation and carrying relief supplies from Juba, South Sudan.</li></ul>\n<p><br />\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operators">Operators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Siddeley_HS_748&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Operators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_operators">Civil operators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Siddeley_HS_748&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Civil operators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As of July 2018 a total of 12 HS 748 aircraft (all variants) remained in airline service. As of September 2018 <a href="/wiki/Transport_Canada" title="Transport Canada">Transport Canada</a> (TC) list 13 HS 748 in Canada with a current Certificate of Registration and 1 with a cancelled certificate.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Current operators are:<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="/wiki/Zambian_Air_Force" title="Zambian Air Force">Zambian Air Force</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span id="Specifications_.28Super_748.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Specifications_(Super_748)">Specifications (Super 748)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Siddeley_HS_748&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Specifications (Super 748)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p style="font-size: 90%; margin:0;"><i>Data from</i> <i>Jane\'s Civil and Military Aircraft Upgrades, 1994\xe2\x80\x9395</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> <i>BAE Systems</i><sup id="cite_ref-bae_heri_3-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bae_heri-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></p><p><span style="font-size: 120%;"><b>General characteristics</b></span>\n</p><ul><li><b>Crew:</b> 2 plus 1 passenger attendant (if required)</li>\n<li><b>Capacity:</b> 40\xe2\x80\x9358 passengers / 11,323&#160;lb (5,136&#160;kg) payload</li>\n<li><b>Length:</b> 67&#160;ft 0&#160;in (20.42&#160;m)</li>\n<li><b>Wingspan:</b> 102&#160;ft 5.5&#160;in (31.229&#160;m)</li>\n<li><b>Height:</b> 24&#160;ft 10&#160;in (7.57&#160;m)</li>\n<li><b>Wing area:</b> 829&#160;sq&#160;ft (77.0&#160;m<sup>2</sup>)</li>\n<li><b>Aspect ratio:</b> 11.967</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Airfoil" title="Airfoil">Airfoil</a>:</b> <b>root:</b> <a href="/wiki/NACA_airfoil" title="NACA airfoil">NACA 23018</a>; <b>tip:</b> <a href="/wiki/NACA_airfoil" title="NACA airfoil">NACA 4412</a><sup id="cite_ref-Selig_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Selig-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Empty weight:</b> 27,126&#160;lb (12,304&#160;kg)</li>\n<li><b>Max takeoff weight:</b> 46,500&#160;lb (21,092&#160;kg)</li>\n<li><b>Fuel capacity:</b> 1,440&#160;imp&#160;gal (1,730&#160;US&#160;gal; 6,500&#160;l) in two wing integral tanks</li>\n<li><b>Powerplant:</b> 2 \xc3\x97 <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_RDa.7_Dart_Mk_536-2" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolls-Royce RDa.7 Dart Mk 536-2">Rolls-Royce RDa.7 Dart Mk 536-2</a> <a href="/wiki/Turboprop" title="Turboprop">turboprop</a> engines, 2,280&#160;shp (1,700&#160;kW)  each equivalent</li>\n<li><b>Propellers:</b> 4-bladed <a href="/wiki/Dowty_Rotol" class="mw-redirect" title="Dowty Rotol">Dowty Rotol</a> constant-speed fully-feathering propellers, 12&#160;ft 0&#160;in (3.66&#160;m) diameter</li></ul>\n<p><span style="font-size: 120%;"><b>Performance</b></span>\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Cruise speed:</b> 244&#160;kn (281&#160;mph, 452&#160;km/h)</li>\n<li><b>Range:</b> 926&#160;nmi (1,066&#160;mi, 1,715&#160;km) (with max payload)</li>\n<li><b>Service ceiling:</b> 25,000&#160;ft (7,600&#160;m)</li>\n<li><b>Wing loading:</b> 56.1&#160;lb/sq&#160;ft (274&#160;kg/m<sup>2</sup>)</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Power-to-weight_ratio" title="Power-to-weight ratio">Power/mass</a>:</b> 0.0981&#160;hp/lb (0.1613&#160;kW/kg)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Preserved_aircraft">Preserved aircraft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Siddeley_HS_748&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Preserved aircraft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Siddeley_HS_748&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A10-601_(16432349288).jpg" class="image"><img alt=""
